             <div class="main section" id="main">
              <div class="widget Blog" id="Blog1">
               <div class="blog-posts hfeed">
                <!-- google_ad_section_start(name=default) -->
                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, October 31, 2012
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                    <meta content="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-jz6FucERayk/UJFSnUPkquI/AAAAAAAAYGE/cDYP7Dgi4d8/photo2_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" itemprop="image_url"/>
                    <meta content="7781670590071996754" itemprop="blogId"/>
                    <meta content="2476283781941765104" itemprop="postId"/>
                    <a name="2476283781941765104">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                     Library bookcases done. Boom!
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2476283781941765104" itemprop="description articleBody">
                     <p>
                      Remember that one time, back in January, when I had that idea to transform our
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/01/dining-room-turned.html">
                       dining room into a library
                      </a>
                      ? And then, back in March, when we started the process of building bookcases for the new library?
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Yeah, it was eight months ago, so I dont blame you if you cant remember. ;) Well, they are finally done!!!! And Im thrilled!!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I have worked my butt off over the past few days to get them done. Seriously, my butt should be a third of its size.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      There was
                      <em>
                       so
                      </em>
                      much to do to finish up, I didnt realize how long it would take. There was a TON of painting  I had done one coat of primer on the bottom cabinets before, but then I dropped a can of blue paint that splattered all over them (fun times) and I got a recommendation to use an oil-based primer instead anyway (more on that later). So, I reprimed the cabinets and taped off the baseboards and cabinet trim with my Frogtape:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-TYvBhH0_K00/UJFSlx2cxNI/AAAAAAAAYF8/uj7oqhWBDWc/s1600-h/photo2%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="300" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-jz6FucERayk/UJFSnUPkquI/AAAAAAAAYGE/cDYP7Dgi4d8/photo2_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I did one more coat of primer and two coats of semi gloss white paint.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I primed the cabinet doors and then sprayed them with the semi gloss two times:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-Fwjs5iP0IBg/UJFSnmwWArI/AAAAAAAAYGM/0os7x4j6B5A/s1600-h/photo%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="328" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-63ANwAoa0gQ/UJFSo0nrtRI/AAAAAAAAYGU/xFe6mJEqNf8/photo_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      The finish is impeccable! Ill show you more of that process soon too!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I used a TON caulk. It was insane. I used this trick I saw on a DIY show. Or maybe it was a blog? Pinterest? Who knows anymore!:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-3k4CcLnJyuY/UJFSpNGr2sI/AAAAAAAAYGc/qwReJGMJzNM/s1600-h/IMG_3417%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="267" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/--SIhH6sNttI/UJFSpyxqtII/AAAAAAAAYGk/SywZodV7KYU/IMG_3417_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="" width="400"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      And found an awesome tool that helped this process immensely that Ill show you soon too!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I installed the crown molding in the room and caulked the top and bottom of that:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-HYv9djQuQrw/UJFSrfobs0I/AAAAAAAAYGs/NNXohIR89x8/s1600-h/IMG_3478%25255B4%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="300" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-iCvwg15N4F0/UJFSr3z0j1I/AAAAAAAAYG0/K_Cx_H9mCiw/IMG_3478_thumb%25255B2%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="" width="450"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I originally picked out hardware that was a nickel finish, but I realized after I got the lights in that I wanted the hardware to match it, so I went back to Home Depot and picked these out:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-CvoKInrHiqU/UJFSs-Zy1UI/AAAAAAAAYG8/CXvL6X4Pl0I/s1600-h/IMG_3457%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" height="480" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-13Guusfj8tg/UJFStoOcvvI/AAAAAAAAYHE/Z4qIijx0H7g/IMG_3457_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I love their clean lines  they say library to me:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-Ju3s8P7dVAg/UJFSt4HLWWI/AAAAAAAAYHM/KMCci8U4Ois/s1600-h/IMG_3455%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="oil rubbed bronze cabinet hardware" border="0" height="480" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-NZrghi2GpOY/UJFSvYd01zI/AAAAAAAAYHU/0fDm-nZ3x3I/IMG_3455_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="oil rubbed bronze cabinet hardware" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I installed some lattice wood on the side of the cabinets just to add a little detail:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-rStM1IRu-XQ/UJFSw-S21nI/AAAAAAAAYHc/PFkyKl_eaXo/s1600-h/IMG_3472%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="trim on side of cabinet" border="0" height="480" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-SMa97eSTOmo/UJFSxbrTQII/AAAAAAAAYHk/rkaLsWTJb_A/IMG_3472_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="trim on side of cabinet" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      And THEN I could really start decorating the shelves! Ive had most of them (mostly) done for awhile now, it was those taller shelves on the bottom that were hard:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-QHb3otCBMzk/UJFSyuy7MDI/AAAAAAAAYHs/9EF2_IJLTWo/s1600-h/IMG_3476%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="dark bronze cabinet hardware " border="0" height="300" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-9tAVQUIPHuw/UJFSzHieFTI/AAAAAAAAYH0/3eMdWtb26EY/IMG_3476_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="dark bronze cabinet hardware " width="450"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Sometimes accessorizing is the easiest thing and everything just falls into places nicely. Sometimes it takes FOREVER to get it right. These took
                      <em>
                       for.ev.er
                      </em>
                      :
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-QPZwzoA4VOg/UJFSzuz84uI/AAAAAAAAYH8/ZmYmetJeTg4/s1600-h/IMG_3469%25255B3%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="accessorizing bookcases" border="0" height="480" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-rYuuh-TxwWo/UJFS0NpHn_I/AAAAAAAAYIE/rAMlj9X9u_8/IMG_3469_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="accessorizing bookcases" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Ill share more detail on all of the accessories soon, but for now, lets just enjoy the final result shall we?:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-6FVa7CvgVTc/UJFS04GUsbI/AAAAAAAAYIM/Ba1i7U2W5JI/s1600-h/IMG_3437%25255B8%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases" border="0" height="680" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-rBUwzy1Ekd4/UJFS1VGkbII/AAAAAAAAYIU/pEWeu-u5uWw/IMG_3437_thumb%25255B6%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="DIY built in bookcases" width="500"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      The dog likes it too. I swear I dont stage him like that  our animals are just obsessed with being in each photo. I had just shooed the cats out of the shot. ;)
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I know I say this a lot, but they turned out EXACTLY how they looked in my head. I really dont think I could be happier:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-HX7AhhyhQ68/UJFS1-f253I/AAAAAAAAYIc/7kCn22xIr_k/s1600-h/IMG_3444%25255B7%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases with cabinet bases" border="0" height="370" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-hXZc0aJ_y1g/UJFS2Hx7eAI/AAAAAAAAYIk/m4xDm8L_PqE/IMG_3444_thumb%25255B5%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="DIY built in bookcases with cabinet bases" width="525"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I love how the shelf spacing turned out  we made the bottom one bigger because we had to deal with the light switch and thermostat. We have a ton of bigger books that I wanted to have room for on the bottom, but I ended up laying them all flat anyway. ;) At first I was a little nervous about the bigger bottom shelf but I really like how it came together.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      By the way, we asked two heating and cooling guys about the thermostat  I thought wed have to move it. They both said its fine as is, which was a nice surprise. Im even more surprised that they dont bother me much. I hardly notice them.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      We have a column in the room that prevents a good straight shot of these, so heres a couple that show more detail of the bookcases:
                     </p>
                     <p align="center">
                      <a href="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-8T2nG5brt-E/UJFS22Hcr8I/AAAAAAAAYIs/2ae_LbuTnSc/s1600-h/IMG_3436%25255B6%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases" border="0" height="458" src="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-0kSZrnDhevQ/UJFS3BC1_2I/AAAAAAAAYI0/uUTusF2q2aE/IMG_3436_thumb%25255B8%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; border-left-width: 0px" title="DIY built in bookcases" width="271"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-qTZlaTeqF60/UJFS3k9W20I/AAAAAAAAYI8/_P5LMB3WrHc/s1600-h/IMG_3435%25255B6%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases" border="0" height="455" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-lbXS9YfTHt8/UJFS5BMLGnI/AAAAAAAAYJE/dhJvGtwprSE/IMG_3435_thumb%25255B7%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: inline; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; border-left-width: 0px" title="DIY built in bookcases" width="286"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      I didnt want to lose much floor space in the room, so we used upper cabinets for the bases  theyre only 12 inches deep. It worked perfectly  I didnt want the shelves to be any deeper than that:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-SB8VROrIWTg/UJFS55e3xWI/AAAAAAAAYJM/16_L2cp273s/s1600-h/IMG_3445%25255B7%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases butcher block" border="0" height="675" src="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-hseH2i8Qn2Q/UJFS78RdDeI/AAAAAAAAYJU/adIsb3Ms--c/IMG_3445_thumb%25255B5%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="DIY built in bookcases butcher block" width="450"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      The cabinets were just the unfinished kind you can find at most big box hardware stores. Even at 12 inches deep they hold a TON! Ill show you
                      <em>
                       that
                      </em>
                      soon too! ;)
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Obviously it took me waaaay longer than I thought it would to build these. Ive never done something this large. Dad helped me a TON by coming by a day or two a month to help me create them -- but I otherwise it was (mostly) me. We had help on one part  adding the trim to the front of the shelves.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Now I cant wait to get moving on the rest of the room! Most of it wont be too bad  Ive had a new light sitting in the garage for months (this one is too ornate for what Im going for in here  its moving elsewhere). The drapes wont be too hard (just have to find the perfect fabric!). Ive already got a coffee table that will go in the middle of the room that will get a redo.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      The chairs are going to be the biggie  finding four, super comfy, pretty,
                      <em>
                       affordable
                      </em>
                      chairs will be interesting. :) My plan is to put the coffee table and four chairs in the middle of the room for another comfy spot to sit:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh3.ggpht.com/-rHHtDWw4chw/UJFS8cksvyI/AAAAAAAAYJc/irAh43xTpGc/s1600-h/IMG_3448%25255B10%25255D.jpg">
                       <font color="#4c4c4c">
                       </font>
                       <img alt="DIY built in library bookcases" border="0" height="749" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-OQSPtvoqZjs/UJFS8zZHGSI/AAAAAAAAYJk/MGXtk-0TB6U/IMG_3448_thumb%25255B8%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="DIY built in library bookcases" width="500"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      We never ever, I mean, never used the dining room. Ever. I do think a dining room table would look lovely in front of the built ins, but I just dont want to go back to a space that we dont use. For now, the chairs are the plan!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Since Im obsessed with before and afters, lets take a look at the room earlier this year:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <img alt="chocolate brown dining room" border="0" height="480" src="http://lh4.ggpht.com/-VvF9v3s-Qho/Tw0FQkjAc9I/AAAAAAAARv8/ERWjZH9ZsRw/IMG_9633_thumb%25255B1%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" title="chocolate brown dining room" width="320"/>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      This was a result of my dark and dramatic phase. ;) I really did love this room, but when I painted it chocolate brown the floor was light carpet. The addition of the hardwoods made it feel like a cave.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Im so thrilled to have a much brighter, useful room now!:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      <a href="http://lh6.ggpht.com/-2BNGT0RNXck/UJFS9btnyOI/AAAAAAAAYJs/YQuZaYZC0ew/s1600-h/IMG_3442%25255B13%25255D.jpg">
                       <img alt="DIY built in bookcases" border="0" height="675" src="http://lh5.ggpht.com/-5tTJ2xpTAbk/UJFS90WsnuI/AAAAAAAAYJ0/Js8-oLEraXQ/IMG_3442_thumb%25255B11%25255D.jpg?imgmax=800" style="border-right-width: 0px; display: block; float: none; border-top-width: 0px; border-bottom-width: 0px; margin-left: auto; border-left-width: 0px; margin-right: auto" title="DIY built in bookcases" width="450"/>
                      </a>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      And for all that is good, I am SO GLAD this part is done!!! :)
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Can I get a
                      <em>
                       <strong>
                        WHOOOOO
                       </strong>
                      </em>
                      ??
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Thanks so much for coming along on this ride with me  and thanks for your patience. I hope you love them and are inspired!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      For more on this project, check out these links:
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      We started out with adding toe kicks to the cabinets and fitting them in place
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/03/dining-room-transformation.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      I pulled down all the trim in the room, had the lights and outlets wired (we had help on that too)
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/04/dining-room-transformation-part-2.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      I installed and primed the cabs, painted the walls (twice, ugh!)
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/05/dining-room-turned-library-progress.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      I showed you how we built the bookcases (frame and shelves)
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/08/how-to-build-built-ins.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      The trim was added and shelves beefed up
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/09/library-built-ins-update-so-close.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      The library light drama was covered
                      <a href="http://thriftydecorchick.blogspot.com/2012/10/library-lights-finally.html">
                       here
                      </a>
                      .
                      <br/>
                      Also, check out my method for decorating these shelves in
                      <a href="http://www.thriftydecorchick.com/2012/11/how-to-accessorize-bookcases.html" target="_blank">
                       this post
                      </a>
                      .
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Whew!! MAJOR props to my Dad for all the help, and my hubby and son for being patient with me for the past few days so I could get er done!
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Now Im off to create a new Halloween costume for a cute little boy. The ninja now wants to be the Headless Horseman and Im determined to make it happen. And thenIm taking a nap. For a few days. ;)
                     </p>

      var config = {'blogId': '7781670590071996754', 'postId': '2476283781941765104', 'feed': 'http://www.thriftydecorchick.com/feeds/2476283781941765104/comments/default', 'authorName': 'Sarah @ Thrifty Decor Chick', 'authorUrl': 'http://www.blogger.com/profile/08387609050626968143', 'baseUri': 'http://www.blogger.com', 'maxThreadDepth': 2};

      var cursor = null;
      if (items &amp;&amp; items.length &gt; 0) {
        cursor = parseInt(items[items.length - 1].timestamp) + 1;
      }

      var bodyFromEntry = function(entry) {
        if (entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
          for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.contentRemoved') {
              return '&lt;span class="deleted-comment"&gt;' + entry.content.$t + '&lt;/span&gt;';
            }
          }
        }
        return entry.content.$t;
      }

      var parse = function(data) {
        cursor = null;
        var comments = [];
        if (data &amp;&amp; data.feed &amp;&amp; data.feed.entry) {
          for (var i = 0, entry; entry = data.feed.entry[i]; i++) {
            var comment = {};
            // comment ID, parsed out of the original id format
            var id = /blog-(\d+).post-(\d+)/.exec(entry.id.$t);
            comment.id = id ? id[2] : null;
            comment.body = bodyFromEntry(entry);
            comment.timestamp = Date.parse(entry.published.$t) + '';
            if (entry.author &amp;&amp; entry.author.constructor === Array) {
              var auth = entry.author[0];
              if (auth) {
                comment.author = {
                  name: (auth.name ? auth.name.$t : undefined),
                  profileUrl: (auth.uri ? auth.uri.$t : undefined),
                  avatarUrl: (auth.gd$image ? auth.gd$image.src : undefined)
                };
              }
            }
            if (entry.link) {
              if (entry.link[2]) {
                comment.link = comment.permalink = entry.link[2].href;
              }
              if (entry.link[3]) {
                var pid = /.*comments\/default\/(\d+)\?.*/.exec(entry.link[3].href);
                if (pid &amp;&amp; pid[1]) {
                  comment.parentId = pid[1];
                }
              }
            }
            comment.deleteclass = 'item-control blog-admin';
            if (entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
              for (var k in entry.gd$extendedProperty) {
                if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.itemClass') {
                  comment.deleteclass += ' ' + entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                } else if (entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].name == 'blogger.displayTime') {
                  comment.displayTime = entry.gd$extendedProperty[k].value;
                }
              }
            }
            comments.push(comment);
          }
        }
        return comments;
      };

      var paginator = function(callback) {
        if (hasMore()) {
          var url = config.feed + '?alt=json&amp;v=2&amp;orderby=published&amp;reverse=false&amp;max-results=50';
          if (cursor) {
            url += '&amp;published-min=' + new Date(cursor).toISOString();
          }
          window.bloggercomments = function(data) {
            var parsed = parse(data);
            cursor = parsed.length &lt; 50 ? null
                : parseInt(parsed[parsed.length - 1].timestamp) + 1
            callback(parsed);
            window.bloggercomments = null;
          }
          url += '&amp;callback=bloggercomments';
          var script = document.createElement('script');
          script.type = 'text/javascript';
          script.src = url;
          document.getElementsByTagName('head')[0].appendChild(script);
        }
      };
      var hasMore = function() {
        return !!cursor;
      };
      var getMeta = function(key, comment) {
        if ('iswriter' == key) {
          var matches = !!comment.author
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.name == config.authorName
              &amp;&amp; comment.author.profileUrl == config.authorUrl;
          return matches ? 'true' : '';
        } else if ('deletelink' == key) {
          return config.baseUri + '/delete-comment.g?blogID='
               + config.blogId + '&amp;postID=' + comment.id;
        } else if ('deleteclass' == key) {
          return comment.deleteclass;
        }
        return '';
      };

      var replybox = null;
      var replyUrlParts = null;
      var replyParent = undefined;

      var onReply = function(commentId, domId) {
        if (replybox == null) {
          // lazily cache replybox, and adjust to suit this style:
          replybox = document.getElementById('comment-editor');
          if (replybox != null) {
            replybox.height = '250px';
            replybox.style.display = 'block';
            replyUrlParts = replybox.src.split('#');
          }
        }
        if (replybox &amp;&amp; (commentId !== replyParent)) {
          document.getElementById(domId).insertBefore(replybox, null);
          replybox.src = replyUrlParts[0]
              + (commentId ? '&amp;parentID=' + commentId : '')
              + '#' + replyUrlParts[1];
          replyParent = commentId;
        }
      };

      var hash = (window.location.hash || '#').substring(1);
      var startThread, targetComment;
      if (/^comment-form_/.test(hash)) {
        startThread = hash.substring('comment-form_'.length);
      } else if (/^c[0-9]+$/.test(hash)) {
        targetComment = hash.substring(1);
      }

      // Configure commenting API:
      var configJso = {
        'maxDepth': config.maxThreadDepth
      };
      var provider = {
        'id': config.postId,
        'data': items,
        'loadNext': paginator,
        'hasMore': hasMore,
        'getMeta': getMeta,
        'onReply': onReply,
        'rendered': true,
        'initComment': targetComment,
        'initReplyThread': startThread,
        'config': configJso,
        'messages': msgs
      };

      var render = function() {
        if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
          var holder = document.getElementById('comment-holder');
          window.goog.comments.render(holder, provider);
        }
      };

      // render now, or queue to render when library loads:
      if (window.goog &amp;&amp; window.goog.comments) {
        render();
      } else {
        window.goog = window.goog || {};
        window.goog.comments = window.goog.comments || {};
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue = window.goog.comments.loadQueue || [];
        window.goog.comments.loadQueue.push(render);

                            <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_67MC">
                             Your solution for an unused room is gorgeous AND practical.  You can't get better than that.  I love the chairs circled around a coffee table or ottoman for comfy reading.  When I tried it here, the issue with floating the furniture in mid-room was no place to plug in reading lamps. I am hoping you have a basement so you can run wiring there and install floor plugs for your lamps. My house is on a slab so no easy way to install floor plugs.  Wires running everywhere really cramped my attempt at style.  Good luck!

                                  <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_136MC">
                                   Hello Karen! I can't remember exactly because we spread it out so long but the base cabinets were $320 and then the other wood for the shelves and trim was probably $150 - $200. Maybe not even that much because we used basic pine for the shelves but nicer pine for the trimwork. I had a little over $100 in lights as well and only paid about $150 for the electrical work. I think the final cost was between $650 - $750. But ours are 12 feet wide so that's for our large version. :) Good luck!!
                                  </p>
